  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b6a5d504-1ab1-4a83-9e36-97cd50765e38'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

But that means traversing stormy seas, surviving a bitter winter, and battling a group of deadly pirates willing to protect their prize at all costs. Even Brotherband training and the help of Skandia's greatest warrior may not be enough to ensure that Hal and his friends return home with the Andomal--or their lives.</span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/87745333-isabela"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1602453687i/87745333._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/87745333-isabela">Isabela</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Flanagan sets this story in a fictional world. However, he draws inspiration for each country and civilization from the real world; most (all, really)<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Flanagan sets this story in a fictional world. However, he draws inspiration for each country and civilization from the real world; most (all, really) can be directly compared to its inspiration. The majority of the book refers to Skandia (a country similar to the Scandinavian countries of the north)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_411451422" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/411451422" />
    <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington"><img alt="Jonathan Terrington" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478230200p2/6313408.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/411451422?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan Terrington" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington">Jonathan Terrington</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781741664508" href="/book/show/15704753-the-invaders">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=children-s-literature">children-s-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi-challenge">fantasy-sci-fi-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=humorous">humorous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=new-ya-books-challenge">new-ya-books-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=favourite-series">favourite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=australian">australian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer411451422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10384752936376891608"><br/>As a YA novel <i>The Invaders</i> is intelligent, entertaining and top of its class. As a novel to recommend for anyone looking for a purely entertaining read it's very worthwhile. John Flanagan, author of the brilliant Rangers Apprentice series (see <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60400.The_Ruins_of_Gorlan__Ranger_s_Apprentice___1_' title='The Ruins of Gorlan (Ranger's Apprentice, #1) by John Flanagan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Ruins of Gorlan</a> one which both I, my mother and my sister - the readers in our house - love) continues the adventures of his young Skandian sailors as they set out to retrieve an artefact lost on their watch and hence their honour.<br/><br/>John Flanagan writes </span>
  <span id="freeText10384752936376891608" style="display:none"><br />As a YA novel <i>The Invaders</i> is intelligent, entertaining and top of its class. As a novel to recommend for anyone looking for a purely entertaining read it's very worthwhile. John Flanagan, author of the brilliant Rangers Apprentice series (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60400.The_Ruins_of_Gorlan__Ranger_s_Apprentice___1_" title="The Ruins of Gorlan (Ranger's Apprentice, #1) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ruins of Gorlan</a> one which both I, my mother and my sister - the readers in our house - love) continues the adventures of his young Skandian sailors as they set out to retrieve an artefact lost on their watch and hence their honour.<br /><br />John Flanagan writes in a manner that is particularly appealing to me personally. I think it has something to do with the mixture of classier words and terms and his easy-going style: he certainly has got the laid-back Australian manner down in his writing. I suspect if I were to compare this to other average YA novels however that the lexicon would prove more advanced, that the language would prove more sophisticated in its elegant construction than those. In fact the wonder of this novel is that I know many younger children who can read these novels and still get plenty out of them. It's remarkable to think that the language in this is perhaps far more advanced than <i>The Hunger Games</i>. Likely only content at this point would separate a ten year old from reading <i>The Hunger Games</i> over this for its simplicity. Although that said <i>The Invaders</i> does feature pirates torturing a captive (although only the after effects are described) and far more deaths than <i>The Hunger Games</i>. Although of course the difference is that in this all the deaths are typically villainous pirates who deserve to die for their evil misdeeds.<br /><br />On the whole this is a YA novel that appears unassuming but is a very entertaining read. In fact I'd rate John Flanagan's entire writing collection (Rangers Apprentice and Brotherband series combined) as some of the finest in YA and modern children's writing in general. If you have ten year-olds to 18 year-olds (particularly boys, but my sister proves that girls will like these) who are looking for a fun fantasy read that's humorous, less taxing than <i>The Hobbit</i> but in the same spirit of medieval style adventure then have a look at these books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10384752936376891608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_335151428" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/335151428" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1350237-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328993102p2/1350237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/335151428?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/1350237-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer335151428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10703385784435730716">John Flanagan is a great author, but this book was SO weighed down with detail that I wanted to pull my hair out by the end. All of the nautical references and tidbits about how they turned the boat or changed the sails just annoyed me. Pages and pages of this stuff and I STILL didn't know what he was talking about! Perhaps it's just me. I've never been on any kind of sailboat and so I have nothing to reference it to. Thus, it becomes mumbo-jumbo to my brain. <br/><br/>I really loved the characters in the</span>
  <span id="freeText10703385784435730716" style="display:none">John Flanagan is a great author, but this book was SO weighed down with detail that I wanted to pull my hair out by the end. All of the nautical references and tidbits about how they turned the boat or changed the sails just annoyed me. Pages and pages of this stuff and I STILL didn't know what he was talking about! Perhaps it's just me. I've never been on any kind of sailboat and so I have nothing to reference it to. Thus, it becomes mumbo-jumbo to my brain. <br /><br />I really loved the characters in the first book and I still love them in this one, but it's starting to feel more and more like "The Rangers Apprentice". Misfit boy shows amazing intelligence and skill beyond his years. Best friend is always by his side through everything. Snarky mentor makes everything as difficult as possible, but is really teaching them great life lessons. And the girl. Tall. Beautiful. Intelligent. It just felt like you could insert Will for Hal... or Horace for Stig... Halt for Thorn and Evanlyn or Alyss for Lydia. They could be interchangeable for the most part.<br /><br />To top it off, this book felt a little unnecessary. The first 200 pages or so are pretty darn slow. The next 200 pick up fairly well, but in the end, the book didn't really go anywhere. It felt like filler. Frustratingly long, drawn out, pointless filler.<br /><br />If I could give this 2.5 stars, I would. Since I can't, I'm rounding up and hoping that the book that's due out in October will be better!!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10703385784435730716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer789512018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8043312763615529051">3.5<br/><br/>Picking up immediately from the end of the first book, with the Herons in search of the Andomal, the beginning of the story was actually a bit slow to get started. See, they end up getting caught heading out during a bad time of year, and have to hole up for awhile to avoid the storms and while there's some character development happening and improvements to the ship, not much happened that felt like it was moving the story forward.<br/><br/>This take a marked turn, though, when the crew of the Heron r</span>
  <span id="freeText8043312763615529051" style="display:none">3.5<br /><br />Picking up immediately from the end of the first book, with the Herons in search of the Andomal, the beginning of the story was actually a bit slow to get started. See, they end up getting caught heading out during a bad time of year, and have to hole up for awhile to avoid the storms and while there's some character development happening and improvements to the ship, not much happened that felt like it was moving the story forward.<br /><br />This take a marked turn, though, when the crew of the Heron rescues a boat at sea - a young woman who escaped the attack of her town by the same pirates they're hunting. From this point forward, things happen at a much better pace, and there's much action and adventure to be had - though, as Flanagan is rather fond of, the story arc doesn't wrap up in this book. It's not a cliffhanger, but the story is far from over. <br /><br />Overall, I don't enjoy this series quite as much as Ranger's Apprentice, and I think a lot of that is I just don't have the same connection to the characters as I do in RA. But they are growing on me, especially Thorn, and I really enjoyed the addition of Lydia to the story. It's nice to see a strong female character added to the case - even if that means there's hints of romance and drama in the air.<br /><br />I do look forward to getting to the next book, and I just hope it's not quite as sluggish in the beginning as this one was.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8043312763615529051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/297446854?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hazel West" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hazel West" href="/user/show/6747285-hazel-west">Hazel West</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6747285-hazel-west?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6747285-hazel-west?shelf=great-summer-reads">great-summer-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6747285-hazel-west?shelf=brothers-in-arms-books">brothers-in-arms-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer297446854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14557943804094209633">I'm not sure I liked this one better than the first book in the series, but it was still good. It was a little more slow-paced than I thought it would be, but it is actually kind of an in-between book with another cliff-hanger at the end. The slow parts in the beginning don't really take away from the story either, they just lend to strengthening the camaraderie between the Herons and it was fun to watch Thorn train them. I'm still not quite sure what I think about Lydia. I almost felt that she </span>
  <span id="freeText14557943804094209633" style="display:none">I'm not sure I liked this one better than the first book in the series, but it was still good. It was a little more slow-paced than I thought it would be, but it is actually kind of an in-between book with another cliff-hanger at the end. The slow parts in the beginning don't really take away from the story either, they just lend to strengthening the camaraderie between the Herons and it was fun to watch Thorn train them. I'm still not quite sure what I think about Lydia. I almost felt that she didn't really have to be necessary. "The Outcasts" did well enough without a lead female role, I think we could have done without one in this book too, but that's my opinion. I was also a little disappointed that Hal and Tursgud didn't get to meet again in this book and settle their problem once and for all, but I bet that will come later. Zavac on the other hand is seriously a great pirate and a worthy villain. He's cold and evil and yet he manages to not be cliche. Now I'm eagerly awaiting the next installment of this series, and I hope it's not too long before it comes out!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14557943804094209633" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Elaine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9225232-elaine"><img alt="Elaine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335987660p2/9225232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2049728326?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elaine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elaine" href="/user/show/9225232-elaine">Elaine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9225232-elaine?shelf=middle-grade-books">middle-grade-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2049728326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1605230783273310581">This was a solid sequel to "The Outcasts." The Herons are on their own now (with Thorn), and I loved seeing how they worked together as a team, anticipating Hal's commands and everyone willing to step in and do their part and cover whatever needs come around. Hal has some brilliant ideas to give them the upper hand in their battle. <br/><br/>The addition of Lydia was nice, she seems interesting enough (very much like Cassandra/Evanlyn-beautiful yet independent and courageous, and also skilled and resource</span>
  <span id="freeText1605230783273310581" style="display:none">This was a solid sequel to "The Outcasts." The Herons are on their own now (with Thorn), and I loved seeing how they worked together as a team, anticipating Hal's commands and everyone willing to step in and do their part and cover whatever needs come around. Hal has some brilliant ideas to give them the upper hand in their battle. <br /><br />The addition of Lydia was nice, she seems interesting enough (very much like Cassandra/Evanlyn-beautiful yet independent and courageous, and also skilled and resourceful with her weapon of choice). I can see the love triangle heating up, which looks to be a fun addition to the series. I do have a problem with how "stunningly beautiful" the leading ladies are in this and in Ranger's Apprentice. I appreciate that they are skilled and courageous, but must outward beauty also be dragged into each major female character? I feel like it is rather sexist(there's no mention of how good-looking Hal or Stig or Will or Halt or Horace are), and also reinforces the idea that girls NEED to be beautiful to be attractive or interesting to men, which is a terrible message to send to young women. They get enough of that from Hollywood and magazines. It also reinforces the idea that men are chiefly attracted by looks only...and maybe, sadly, that's true? I don't know, I'm not a man. <br /><br />Also, I really enjoyed the character of Thorn-his backstory, his downfall, his recovery, his renewed purpose. In this book (compared to the first book), he's more his own personality, and less like a 're-invention of Halt, with a different backstory.' <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1605230783273310581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_342293417" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/342293417" />
    <a title="Barb Middleton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4361541-barb-middleton"><img alt="Barb Middleton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329182394p2/4361541.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/342293417?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barb Middleton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barb Middleton" href="/user/show/4361541-barb-middleton">Barb Middleton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4361541-barb-middleton?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer342293417" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1357951572452277840">Book one ends with Hal and his crew of sailors fleeing in disgrace from the city they grew up in order to retrieve the Andromal, the sacred artifact of the Skandians, that was stolen by pirates when Hal's crew was supposedly guarding it (they fell asleep). Hal knows that they will be pursued and dragged back home to be punished for leaving the city. They flee under cover of a storm and find a sheltered inlet where Thorn, an adult Skandian warrior who came with on the crew, begins training them o</span>
  <span id="freeText1357951572452277840" style="display:none">Book one ends with Hal and his crew of sailors fleeing in disgrace from the city they grew up in order to retrieve the Andromal, the sacred artifact of the Skandians, that was stolen by pirates when Hal's crew was supposedly guarding it (they fell asleep). Hal knows that they will be pursued and dragged back home to be punished for leaving the city. They flee under cover of a storm and find a sheltered inlet where Thorn, an adult Skandian warrior who came with on the crew, begins training them on how to fight like warriors. The young boys are no match for pirates and the training is intense. When they discover a girl, Lydia, in a boat adrift at sea they find out that the pirates they are seeking have taken over her town and are pillaging it of emeralds found in a nearby mine. Hal must put together a plan to defeat the pirates and give the town back to the villagers.<br /><br />Flanagan loves weapons and shines when describing the use and function of them. Hal invents a crossbow that he mounts on his sailing ship, as well as, a way for his sailing ship to go faster in the water. Lydia is an expert using a dart throwing weapon called an atlatl. Flanagan's writing reminds me of nonfiction texts at times. He's good at descriptions, setting and action; less good with interesting word choices and internal character development. He has his usual humor and banter but I didn't think it worked quite as well in this story because it was between adults and boys. Usually he has the banter between adults and if it's with the boys they don't get it half the time and that makes it funnier.<br /><br />The characters are distinct and have flaws although Hal doesn't really change much from the beginning to the end of the story. Thorn actually changes more becoming the warrior he once was and finding a purpose in his life. Ingvar is interesting as well. His eyesight is so bad that he is almost blind and Thorn teaches him to fight by feel not sight.<br /><br />Lydia uses darts for a weapon because the crossbows are difficult for women to master since the physical strength necessary to pull them back is lacking in most females. Flanagan is an archer and I like that he is realistic on this point. While I read and see movies where women will perform impossible physical feats and I usually just go with it; it was refreshing to have this aspect presented realistically. That's why I raised my eyebrows when  Lydia hits the oil sack on a moving boat with no practice. Would she be able to do that?  Also, I found it unbelievable that the adults wouldn't give input into the strategy for attacking the village against the pirates. Hal does all the planning and the adult warriors don't really add anything to it. I would have thought it would be a group effort, not just the one brilliant young kid in the form of Hal, coming up with the entire scheme.<br /><br />There is plenty of action and violence. They are at war so there is some torture and deaths. The details are not graphic but there are quite a few deaths. An entertaining read.<br /><br />Reading Level 5.8</span>
  <a data-text-id="1357951572452277840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer326501821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15606870442604997651"><a href='http://www.goodreadingguide.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334437i/693717.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>Impressive. Flanagan has a talent for turning sequels into great stories in their own right, and The Invaders doesn't disappoint. In fact, the character development, friendships, battle strategies and action scenes are almost better than the first book in this series.<br/><br/>Though written in the third person, the story has the tone of an older person laughingly retelling the adventures of young friends, perhaps someone like Thorn, appreciating their bravery and daring, and not esteeming them less f</span>
  <span id="freeText15606870442604997651" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.goodreadingguide.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334437i/693717.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Impressive. Flanagan has a talent for turning sequels into great stories in their own right, and The Invaders doesn't disappoint. In fact, the character development, friendships, battle strategies and action scenes are almost better than the first book in this series.<br><br>Though written in the third person, the story has the tone of an older person laughingly retelling the adventures of young friends, perhaps someone like Thorn, appreciating their bravery and daring, and not esteeming them less for their weaknesses and youthful mistakes. There's so much wisdom in the detail, such as that time at the beginning when the boys are restless waiting for their adventure to begin and Thorn advises a strict routine of exercise and hard work, followed by a good night's sleep and more exercise. The result is an immediate improvement in the atmosphere, with boredom relieved and a sense of purpose regained.<br><br>Individual characters too take giant steps. Stig has come a long way in not letting his temper get the better of him, now able to stare down an opponent without hitting him at first provocation. Hal has learned the painful consequences of a commander's choices for his men, realising that he cannot always protect those following his orders from being harmed. Thorn has exposed the hurts and failings of his past in order to begin again anew, and even Ulf and Wulf have transformed their twins' bickering into an acutely synchronised readiness for Hal's command.<br><br>In fact, all of the Brotherband boys' flawed nobility is contrasted strongly with Barat's self-centred bravado and the pirates' cowardly bullying. Hal's boys each have their own temperament and skills, and each follow their own path towards heroism.<br><br>An evenly paced action-character story for boys, but all readers of character driven action adventure will find it an enjoyable read. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.GoodReadingGuide.com">www.GoodReadingGuide.com</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1603447572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16516615864169767804"> This book had an interesting storyline, but was one of those books in a series that doesn't move it forward very much. The only thing the book really did was to introduce a new character. <br/> About the character, I must admit that while she had some fun traits, I don't think her personality was very developed. When she has a major loss, we didn't really see any sadness. Besides that, Flanagan tried to make her tough by having her complain about a person who liked her. Combined with some other trai</span>
  <span id="freeText16516615864169767804" style="display:none"> This book had an interesting storyline, but was one of those books in a series that doesn't move it forward very much. The only thing the book really did was to introduce a new character. <br /> About the character, I must admit that while she had some fun traits, I don't think her personality was very developed. When she has a major loss, we didn't really see any sadness. Besides that, Flanagan tried to make her tough by having her complain about a person who liked her. Combined with some other traits this could have been endearing, but since she didn't seem to react to much else besides boys, it made her seem shallow. Hopefully he will focus more on her in the next book. <br /> One thing I noticed in this book that I hadn't noticed before in the author's writing was he seemed to forget his characters. Something would happen and he would describe a few of the people, but didn't widen to include everyone which made you wonder what happened to the character that a moment ago had been on board the ship.<br /> Another thing that I have found in Flanagan's books are how his characters seem to enjoy killing. I know that they are Skandians (vikings) and he does mention once that they are not cold-blooded killers, but they seemed cruel as they looked forward to maiming people. Also, some of the younger characters, when killing someone for the first time, didn't seem to be remorseful at all. I would expect someone who was painted to be as sensitive as the main character would feel a slight twinge when cutting someone down. <br /> Overall though, this book was an enjoyable read. I think the author would improve his story by fleshing out his characters more, but it is an exciting read and good for a light book over break.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16516615864169767804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2853407180" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2853407180" />
    <a title="Denae Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/857888-denae-christine"><img alt="Denae Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446784625p2/857888.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2853407180?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denae Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denae Christine" href="/user/show/857888-denae-christine">Denae Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/857888-denae-christine?shelf=magicless-fantasy">magicless-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2853407180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9095085245150281572"><b>Reader thoughts:</b> I liked seeing the practical advice from Thorn to Hal (don't let your crew get bored and complain and fight each other! Keep them busy!) and other leadership tips. I liked seeing Hal struggle with how to keep his band together. I liked seeing how they made allies.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[When Stig punched the local snob when he wouldn't let him rescue Hal from the ocean, it was priceless! I loved it! Sometimes, you just have to punch the other guy even if it causes problems later. I like </span></span>
  <span id="freeText9095085245150281572" style="display:none"><b>Reader thoughts:</b> I liked seeing the practical advice from Thorn to Hal (don't let your crew get bored and complain and fight each other! Keep them busy!) and other leadership tips. I liked seeing Hal struggle with how to keep his band together. I liked seeing how they made allies.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When Stig punched the local snob when he wouldn't let him rescue Hal from the ocean, it was priceless! I loved it! Sometimes, you just have to punch the other guy even if it causes problems later. I like me a book where a main character isn't afraid to use some force when it is necessary. It's not like he permanently harmed him. And the local was going to let Hal drown for no reason.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I didn't really like Lydia. She didn't seem to fit the story, more thrown in just because Flanagan wanted a girl in the book. She keeps choosing to run around with the brotherband, and they keep letting her. Really? She's not worried about being the only female on a shipful of young, strange men? Neat that she is so good with her darts, though.<br /><br /><b>Writer thoughts:</b> Flanagan's technique of switching to the bad guys' pov is useful in several ways.<br />1st, it raises tension for the reader when the protagonist may seem to be doing nothing by showing the progress of the enemy.<br />2nd, it shows that the bad guys are competent even if the good guy wins the round by detailing the bad guys' reactions and strategies.<br />3rd, it can raise the stakes with dramatic irony by showing the bad guys planning to thwart/trap the protagonists, who know nothing.<br /><br />If you choose to use this technique, however, keep the scenes short so as to not bog down the story with unnecessary length.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9095085245150281572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1637965233" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1637965233" />
    <a title="Emma Clement" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21467217-emma-clement"><img alt="Emma Clement" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512516342p2/21467217.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1637965233?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Clement" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Clement" href="/user/show/21467217-emma-clement">Emma Clement</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21467217-emma-clement?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1637965233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5337931292471699345">I had a problem with the first book in this series, which was the lack of female characters in the story. Thankfully, Flanagan fixed that(ish) in this one! For the first 166 pages, there was not a single female character (not even a minor one). That was seriously lacking and disappointing. However, a badass female character (that is not a minor one), who challenges gender roles, is introduced in this novel! She is still the only female character who has a part in this story (I think the only oth</span>
  <span id="freeText5337931292471699345" style="display:none">I had a problem with the first book in this series, which was the lack of female characters in the story. Thankfully, Flanagan fixed that(ish) in this one! For the first 166 pages, there was not a single female character (not even a minor one). That was seriously lacking and disappointing. However, a badass female character (that is not a minor one), who challenges gender roles, is introduced in this novel! She is still the only female character who has a part in this story (I think the only other female even mentioned in this story is Hal's mother). But one female character with a strong role is much, much better than only minor female characters in traditional roles (like in the first book of this series). Yes, I do understand that this is a story of a band of boys that are sailors/warriors and in their world, women did have traditional gender roles (and would not have really been in the picture in a brotherband sailing around), I still think that there should be more mention of females and more female characters in the series. So while there is still room for improvement, I think Flanagan definitely made a step in the right direction with the addition of Lydia. BTW I really like her (she has a lot of spunk).<br /><br />Aside from the whole female-lack-aspect of this story, it was a great tale! It incorporates action and fighting, braininess and inventiveness and clever strategy, a 'bad guy' whom it is easy to root against, and more. A great adventure book, and a series I will definitely continue to read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5337931292471699345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_396285491" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/396285491" />
    <a title="Nicolas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12040272-nicolas"><img alt="Nicolas" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/396285491?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicolas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicolas" href="/user/show/12040272-nicolas">Nicolas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer396285491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12818558350444856487">The Invaders, written by John Flanagan, is the second in the Brotherband Chronicles, a series I would recommend to both casual readers and those who truly want a story to sink their teeth in. I highly recommend it to any who have read the Ranger's Apprentice series or the first in the Brotherband Chronicles. I loved this story, taking a take on fantasy without magic and with themes more akin to medieval times, this book is a nice refresher and great for a change in pace for all fantasy book love</span>
  <span id="freeText12818558350444856487" style="display:none">The Invaders, written by John Flanagan, is the second in the Brotherband Chronicles, a series I would recommend to both casual readers and those who truly want a story to sink their teeth in. I highly recommend it to any who have read the Ranger's Apprentice series or the first in the Brotherband Chronicles. I loved this story, taking a take on fantasy without magic and with themes more akin to medieval times, this book is a nice refresher and great for a change in pace for all fantasy book lovers.<br /><br />It picks up where the first left it. The Andomal, greatest of the Skandians' relics, has been stolen. The Herons, a group of boys who are responsible for its loss, are after the pirate who stole it. They must succeed if they wish to have any lives at all but, along the way, they must first learn to work as a team and train themselves for the desperate fight they will most surely encounter with the pirate.<br /><br />Thorn, an old sea wolf, has come with the boys. He was once the greatest fighter of the Skandians and it falls to him to train them. This he does, surprising each of them with his skill, skill that they, being young, had never seen from the crippled drunk. The Herons have a lot of work but they begin moving in the right track but, their is a Skandian ship sent after them. What are the intentions of the Skandians whom they have fled from to regain their honor? Are they going to help the boys or drag them back in defense? Read this amazing book by Flanagan to find out!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12818558350444856487" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer945348583752852669">This action-packed fantasy novel about a young group of shipmates who are out to recover a stolen artifact will probably sit well with young fans of Flanagan, since it has all the major ingredients still intact: a squeaky clean action/adventure fantasy story with no magic, just set in a different world. I found myself not enjoying it nearly as much as I did the first book in the series, though - maybe I wasn't in the mood for it, since I noticed a lot of writing that felt clunky, and a lot of te</span>
  <span id="freeText945348583752852669" style="display:none">This action-packed fantasy novel about a young group of shipmates who are out to recover a stolen artifact will probably sit well with young fans of Flanagan, since it has all the major ingredients still intact: a squeaky clean action/adventure fantasy story with no magic, just set in a different world. I found myself not enjoying it nearly as much as I did the first book in the series, though - maybe I wasn't in the mood for it, since I noticed a lot of writing that felt clunky, and a lot of telling rather than showing going on. But, flaws like that don't tend to deter the kids very much, so I think this will definitely be in demand at my library.</span>

  <span id="freeText10304808748233161170" style="display:none">Hal and his rogue gang from the Heron brotherband, assisted by Thorn, set off on Hal's boat to recover the Skandian's treasured Andomal from the pirate Zavac, which was stolen due to Hal's mistake. Zavac and his crew on the Raven capture a ship and torture the captain to reveal that a port town (Limmat) has an emerald mine. Capturing the city by subterfuge, a few locals escape to the marsh, including the beautiful, resourceful Lydia, who is rescued by Hal and his crew. The oberjarl sends off a team to help Hal, and under Hal's masterful plan, they attack the pirates in Limmat; however, Hal is forced to rescue the Wolfwind and forego his prize. More action packed than the first book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10304808748233161170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fjZqrkMQHKJX+jtDDyyA9xOzF0JSn+t0EUAuG1VTGmEAt5CyBnSwa/bBTbX/jYZkYWMkcNI5Mo1tNG3KFItHxw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

  <span id="freeText10542721651807000154" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br /><br />For mysteries by this same author, see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8307827.John_A__Flanagan" title="John A. Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">John A. Flanagan</a>.<br /><br />John Flanagan grew up in Sydney, Australia, hoping to be a writer. It wasn't until he wrote a highly uncomplimentary poem about a senior executive at the agency where he worked, however, that his talent was revealed. It turned out one of the company directors agreed with John's assessment of the executive, and happily agreed to train John in copywriting. <br /><br />After writing advertising copy for the next two decades, John teamed with an old friend to develop a television sitcom, Hey Dad!, which went on to air for eight years. <br /><br />John began writing Ranger's Apprentice for his son, Michael, ten years ago, and is still hard at work on the series. <br /><br />He currently lives in a suburb of Manly, Australia, with his wife. In addition to their son, they have two grown daughters and four grandsons.</span>
